Dirhams in Division: Consent Required, Necessity Exception
Matn ruling with commentary explaining the consent requirement and the necessity exception for buildings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule governing the inclusion of dirhams in real estate division and identify the condition that permits it without consent.

Core Idea
Dirhams cannot be forced into division; all partners must consent, except when division of buildings makes it necessary.

This lesson focuses on a key ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq: dirhams (monetary compensation) are not automatically part of joint property division. The commentary explains why and then discusses an exception for buildings, where dirhams become necessary to achieve equality. We'll analyze the condition of consent and the scope of necessity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling from the matn
Read the matn: 'Dirhams are not included in division except with their consent.' This is the foundational rule.
The ruling is absolute; consent of all co-owners is required.
2
Understand the rationale
The commentary explains that dirhams are not part of the common property; including them without consent creates imbalance (one gets real property now, the other gets a debt that may be lost).
3
Recognize the exception for buildings
When land has a building, equality cannot be achieved by area alone. Abu Yusuf requires division by value with dirham compensation; Muhammad requires returning equivalent land. Dirhams are allowed out of necessity to achieve equality.
The exception applies only when necessity arises, i.e., when land is insufficient to compensate building owner.
4
Distinguish between the two positions
Abu Yusuf: always use dirhams to equalize when building is involved. Muhammad: use land first, dirhams only if land insufficient. The text prefers Muhammad's view as it aligns with the original narration (رواية الأصل).
The mufta bihi position follows the original narration, allowing dirhams only when necessary.
5
Note the principle: necessity permits deviation
The rule that dirhams are not included except by consent is relaxed only when essential for fairness in division of indivisible assets like buildings.
This is an application of the maxim 'necessity makes the prohibited permissible' (الضرورة تبيح المحظور).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (ولا تدخل في القسمة الدراهم إلا برضاهم) يعني جماعة في أيديهم عقار فطلبوا القسمة وفي أحد الجانبين فضل عن الآخر فأراد أحدهم أن يدفع عوضه من الدراهم والآخر لم يرض بذلك لم تدخل الدراهم في القسمة لأنه لا شريك له فيها ويفوت به التعديل في القسمة لأن بعضهم يصل إلى عين المال المشترك في الحال ودراهم الآخر في الذمة فيخشى عليها التوى، وإذا كان أرض وبناء فعن الثاني أنه يقسم باعتبار القيمة لأنه يمكن اعتبار التعديل فيه إلا بالتقويم لأن تعديل البناء لا يمكن إلا بالمساحة والمساحة هي الأصل الممسوحات، ثم يرد من وقع البناء في نصيبه قيمة البناء أو من كان أجود دراهم على الآخر فتدخل الدراهم في القسمة ضرورة كالأخ لا ولاية له في المال ثم يملك تسمية الصداق ضرورة صحة التزويج. وعن محمد أنه يرد على شريكه بمقابلة البناء ما يساويه من العرصة، وإذا بقي فضل ولم يمكن تحقيق التسوية فيه بأن لم تف العرصة بقيمة البناء فحينئذ ترد الدارهم لأن الضرورة في هذا القدر فلا يترك الأصل وهو القسمة بالمساحة إلا في هذا . بالضرورة، وهذا يوافق رواية الأصل. وفي المحيط : ولو رفع القسمة على أن يزيد أحدهما شيئاً معلوماً فلا يخلو إما أن يكون المشروط دراهم أو دنانير أو مكيلاً أو موزوناً أو عروضاً أو حيواناً، فإن كان المشروط دراهم معلومة جاز بأن كانت مشروطة لتعديل الأنصباء فيجوز بالتراضي، وإن كانت الزيادة مشروطة لتقع القسمة على المفاضلة فيكون بيعاً من كل وجه وهو جائز بتراضيهما، وإن كانت الزيادة مكيلاً أو موزوناً ولم يسم مكان الإيفاء لم تجز عند الإمام، وعندهما تجوز ويسلمها عند الدار كما في السلم وإن كانت الزيادة عرضاً يجوز السلم فيها كالثوب جاز مؤجلاً ولا يجوز حالاً، وإن كان عروضاً لا يجوز السلم فيه، وإن كان حيواناً بعينه جاز، وبغير عينه لا يجوز . ثلاثة بينهم دور صغرى وكبرى فأخذ أحدهم الكبرى على أن يرد على الآخرين دراهم مسماة جاز، وكذلك لو أخذ الكبرى بنصيبين والصغرى بنصيب جاز. ولو اقتسموا الباب على أن من أصابه هذا رد درهماً، ومن أصابه رد در همین جاز. ولو اقتسموا الأراضي على أن من أصابه شجر ونبت في أرضه فعليه بقيمته دراهم جاز، ولو اقتسما على أن لأحدهما الصامت وللآخر العروض والنحاس والدين على أنه إن بقي عليه شيء من الدين يرد عليه نصفه فالقسمة فاسدة اهـ .
He (the author) said: (Dirhams are not included in the division except with their consent). Meaning: there is a group who own real estate and seek division. In one side there is an excess over the other, so one of them wants to pay compensation with dirhams but the other is not satisfied. Dirhams are not included in the division because the other has no share in them, and equality in division would be lost because one gets actual joint property immediately while the other gets dirhams as a debt, which risks loss. If there is land and a building, according to the second (Abu Yusuf), it is divided based on value because equality can only be achieved through valuation. Building equality cannot be achieved except through measurement, and measurement is the original for measured items. Then the one who gets the building in his share pays the value of the building or the better dirhams to the other. So dirhams are included out of necessity, like a brother who has no authority over money but can specify the dower out of necessity for the validity of marriage. According to Muhammad, he returns to his partner an amount of land equal to the building. If there is a remaining excess and equality cannot be achieved because the land is insufficient for the building's value, then dirhams are given due to necessity, and the original principle of division by measurement is not abandoned except in this case. This agrees with the original narration. In al-Muhit: if they raise the division with one adding something known, it does not vacillate: if the condition is a known amount of dirhams, it is valid if it is for equalizing shares by mutual consent. If the increase is for unequal division, it is a sale from every aspect and is valid with mutual consent. If the increase is a measurable or weighable item without specifying the place of delivery, it is not valid according to Abu Hanifa, but valid according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and delivery is at the house as in salam. If the increase is a commodity like a garment, it is valid as deferred but not immediate. If it is an animal by specification, valid; without specification, invalid. Three persons have small and large houses; one takes the large on condition of giving a named amount of dirhams to the other two, valid. Similarly if he takes the large for two shares and the small for one share, valid. If they divide a door such that whoever gets this returns a dirham, and whoever gets that returns a dirham, valid. If they divide lands such that whoever gets trees and plants in his land must pay their value in dirhams, valid. If two divide such that one gets the silent property and the other gets the goods, copper, and debt, on condition that if any debt remains, he returns half, the division is invalid. End of quote.
Source pages p. 277

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq: dirhams (silver coins) are not included in the division of real estate except with the consent of all partners. The commentary explains the rationale: dirhams are not part of the common property, and including them would create an imbalance because some receive actual land while others receive a debt (dirhams) that may be subject to loss. The text then discusses exceptions: in the case of land with a building, the Hanafi scholars have different opinions. Abu Yusuf holds that division should be by value, and the partner who receives the building must pay compensation (in dirhams) to the other. This is a necessity because buildings cannot be divided by area equally. Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that the partner should return an equivalent area of land to the other. If the land is insufficient, then dirhams are used out of necessity. The original principle of division by area is maintained as far as possible. The passage then quotes from al-Muhit, detailing various scenarios where an additional payment is agreed upon to equalize shares. These are valid by mutual consent, provided the additional item is specified and the conditions of sale are met (e.g., for measurable items, the place of delivery must be specified). Several examples are given: dividing houses with compensating dirhams, dividing land with compensation for trees, etc. The ruling concludes that if the division involves a condition that is invalid (like returning half of a remaining debt, which is uncertain), the division is fasid (void). The authority_weight is from the matn and the commentary, reflecting the established Hanafi position.

Key Terms
دراهم (daraahim): Silver coins used as currency; here representing monetary compensation in division.
قسمة (qisma): Division of joint property among co-owners.
تعديل (ta'dil): Equalization of shares so that each partner receives an equivalent value or area.
ضرورة (darura): Necessity; a legal concept that permits otherwise prohibited actions to achieve a valid outcome.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the default condition for including dirhams in the division of real estate?
A) Dirhams can be included only if the property is a building on land.
B) Dirhams can be included only with the consent of all partners.
C) Dirhams can be included only if the property is a commercial shop.
D) Dirhams can be included only if the debtor agrees.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, dirhams are not part of joint property division without all partners' consent; the building necessity exception permits them only when land compensation is impossible.

Agreed Payments in Division: Conditions and Validity
Expanded discussion from al-Muhit on the validity of conditions in division involving additional payments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the validity of various conditions for compensating payments in property division according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
When partners agree to add dirhams or other items to equalize division, the validity depends on specification, timing, and the nature of the item.

The second part of this passage from al-Muhit details many scenarios where co-owners agree to supplementary payments to balance shares. We will examine the conditions that make such agreements valid or invalid, including the rules for measurable items, commodities, and animals, and the effect of uncertainty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle
Al-Muhit states that if the division is raised with one partner adding a known item, it can be for equalization (ta'dil) or for imbalance (sale).
If for equalization, it is valid by mutual consent; if for imbalance, it is a sale and must meet all sale conditions.
2
Analyze the case of dirhams
If the added item is a known amount of dirhams for equalization, it is valid. If for imbalance, it is a sale and also valid with mutual consent.
3
Examine measurable/weighable items
If the added item is measurable (kayl) or weighable (wazn) without specifying the place of delivery, Abu Hanifa rules it invalid; the Sahibayn allow it with delivery at the house, analogous to salam.
Place of delivery is crucial for these items to avoid uncertainty.
4
Consider commodities and animals
If the addition is a commodity (e.g., cloth), it is valid as deferred sale; for animals, it is valid if the animal is specified, invalid if unspecified.
5
Recognize invalid conditions
The text ends with an example: dividing assets with a condition that if debt remains, the partner returns half. This is uncertain (gharar) and makes the division fasid (void).
Uncertainty (gharar) invalidates the contract.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (ولا تدخل في القسمة الدراهم إلا برضاهم) يعني جماعة في أيديهم عقار فطلبوا القسمة وفي أحد الجانبين فضل عن الآخر فأراد أحدهم أن يدفع عوضه من الدراهم والآخر لم يرض بذلك لم تدخل الدراهم في القسمة لأنه لا شريك له فيها ويفوت به التعديل في القسمة لأن بعضهم يصل إلى عين المال المشترك في الحال ودراهم الآخر في الذمة فيخشى عليها التوى، وإذا كان أرض وبناء فعن الثاني أنه يقسم باعتبار القيمة لأنه يمكن اعتبار التعديل فيه إلا بالتقويم لأن تعديل البناء لا يمكن إلا بالمساحة والمساحة هي الأصل الممسوحات، ثم يرد من وقع البناء في نصيبه قيمة البناء أو من كان أجود دراهم على الآخر فتدخل الدراهم في القسمة ضرورة كالأخ لا ولاية له في المال ثم يملك تسمية الصداق ضرورة صحة التزويج. وعن محمد أنه يرد على شريكه بمقابلة البناء ما يساويه من العرصة، وإذا بقي فضل ولم يمكن تحقيق التسوية فيه بأن لم تف العرصة بقيمة البناء فحينئذ ترد الدارهم لأن الضرورة في هذا القدر فلا يترك الأصل وهو القسمة بالمساحة إلا في هذا . بالضرورة، وهذا يوافق رواية الأصل. وفي المحيط : ولو رفع القسمة على أن يزيد أحدهما شيئاً معلوماً فلا يخلو إما أن يكون المشروط دراهم أو دنانير أو مكيلاً أو موزوناً أو عروضاً أو حيواناً، فإن كان المشروط دراهم معلومة جاز بأن كانت مشروطة لتعديل الأنصباء فيجوز بالتراضي، وإن كانت الزيادة مشروطة لتقع القسمة على المفاضلة فيكون بيعاً من كل وجه وهو جائز بتراضيهما، وإن كانت الزيادة مكيلاً أو موزوناً ولم يسم مكان الإيفاء لم تجز عند الإمام، وعندهما تجوز ويسلمها عند الدار كما في السلم وإن كانت الزيادة عرضاً يجوز السلم فيها كالثوب جاز مؤجلاً ولا يجوز حالاً، وإن كان عروضاً لا يجوز السلم فيه، وإن كان حيواناً بعينه جاز، وبغير عينه لا يجوز . ثلاثة بينهم دور صغرى وكبرى فأخذ أحدهم الكبرى على أن يرد على الآخرين دراهم مسماة جاز، وكذلك لو أخذ الكبرى بنصيبين والصغرى بنصيب جاز. ولو اقتسموا الباب على أن من أصابه هذا رد درهماً، ومن أصابه رد در همین جاز. ولو اقتسموا الأراضي على أن من أصابه شجر ونبت في أرضه فعليه بقيمته دراهم جاز، ولو اقتسما على أن لأحدهما الصامت وللآخر العروض والنحاس والدين على أنه إن بقي عليه شيء من الدين يرد عليه نصفه فالقسمة فاسدة اهـ .

Key Terms
مكيل (makil): A measured by volume (e.g., grain).
موزون (mawzun): A weighed item (e.g., gold, silver).
عرض (arad): Commodity or goods (plural: a'rad).
سلم (salam): A forward sale where payment is made in advance for deferred delivery of specified goods.
فاسد (fasid): Void in the sense of being imperfect; here, the division is invalid and must be redone.

According to the passage from al-Muhit, under what condition is the addition of a measurable item (like wheat) valid in a division agreement according to Abu Hanifa?
A) It is always valid with mutual consent.
B) It is valid only if the place of delivery is specified.
C) It is valid only if the item is weighed at the time of division.
D) It is never valid because measurable items cannot be used in division.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi division law, agreed compensatory payments are valid when the item is specified and free of uncertainty; invalid conditions render the entire division fasid.

Rights of Passage and Water Channel in Division
Ruling on division when a co-owner has a right of passage or water channel over another's share

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on division when one co-owner has a right of passage or water channel over another's share, and explain why rescission occurs if redirection is impossible.

Core Idea
A division must achieve complete independence; if a right of way cannot be removed, the division is rescinded.

In Hanafi fiqh, the purpose of dividing jointly owned property is to give each partner exclusive and independent ownership. But what if one partner has a right to pass through the other's portion? This lesson examines the ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq: the right must be redirected if possible; otherwise, the division is rescinded. We also explore how the road itself may be treated in the division.

Guided Path
1
Identify the right and the division
Determine whether one co-owner has a pre-existing right of way (ṭarīq) or water channel (masīl) over the other's share.
If no such right exists, the division proceeds normally.
2
Check if redirection is possible
If the right can be moved to a different location without harming the right-holder, the division must include that redirection.
The right is re-established on the new path.
3
Apply the ruling: rescission if impossible
If the right cannot be redirected, the division is rescinded (faskh) because its purpose — complete benefit and independence — cannot be achieved.
Contrast with sale, where immediate use is not a condition.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi difference on dividing the road
Some Hanafi authorities hold that the road itself is not divided but remains common; the judge may create a new common road if needed.
This reflects the principle of completing benefit (takmīl al-manfaʿah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وإن قسم ولأحدهم مسيل أو طريق في ملك الآخر لم يشترط في القسمة صرف عنه إن أمكن وإلا فسخت القسمة) لأن المقصود من القسمة تكميل المنفعة باختصاص كل بنصيبه وقطع أسباب تعلق حق الغير فإذا أمكن حصل المقصود وإلا لم يحصل فتعين الفسخ والاستئناف لنفي ضرر الاختلاط بخلاف البيع حيث لا يفسخ ولا يفسد فيما إذا لم يتمكن المشتري من الاستطراق ومن مسيل الطريق الماء لأن المقصود ملك الرقبة ولا يشترط فيه الانتفاع في الحال ولا كذلك القسمة. ولو ذكر الحقوق في الوجه الأول وهو ما إذا أمكن صرفه عن الآخر بأن قال هذا لك بحقوقه كان الجواب فيه مثل ما إذا لم يقل بحقوقه فيصرف عنه إن أمكن كما تقدم إلا إذا قال خذ هذا بطريقه وشربه ومسيله فحينئذ لا يصرف عنه لأنه أثبت له بأبلغ وجوه الإثبات بخلاف البيع إذا ذكر فيه الحقوق حيث يدخل فيه ما كان من الطريق والمسيل فيدخل عند التنصيص. واختلفوا في إدخال الطريق في القسمة بأن قال بعضهم لا يقسم الطريق بل يبقى مشتركاً مثل ما كان قبل القسمة ينظر فيه الحاكم؛ فإن كان يستقيم أن يفتح كل في نصيبه قسم الحاكم من غير طريق يرفع الجماعتهم تكميلا للمنفعة وتحقيقاً للإقرار من كل وجه، وإن كان لا يستقيم ذلك رفع طريقاً بين جماعتهم لتحقق تكميل المنفعة فيما وراء الطريق. ولو اختلفوا في مقدار عرضه يجعل على قدر عرض الباب بطوله أي ارتفاعه حتى يخرج كل واحد جناحاً في نصيبه إن كان فوق الباب لا فيما دونه لأن باب الدار طريق متفق عليه والمختلف فيه يرد إلى المتفق عليه، وفي هذا القدر كفاية في الدخول. ولو شرطوا أن يكون منهم
He (the author) said: (If they divide and one of them has a water channel or road in the property of another, and it was not mentioned in the division, it is redirected away if possible; otherwise the division is rescinded). Because the purpose of division is to complete benefit by each having exclusive use and cutting off causes of attachment of others' rights. If possible, the purpose is achieved; otherwise it is not, so rescission and restart are determined to eliminate the harm of mixture. Unlike sale, where if the buyer cannot access a road or water channel, the sale is not rescinded or invalidated because the purpose is ownership of the corpus, and immediate use is not a condition. That is not the case with division. If the rights were mentioned in the first case, where redirection is possible, and he said 'This is yours with its rights', the answer is similar to if he did not mention rights: it is redirected if possible, unless he said 'Take this with its road, water, and channel', then it is not redirected because he affirmed it in the strongest way. Unlike sale, if rights are mentioned, the road and channel are included only by explicit mention. They differed about including the road in the division. Some say the road is not divided but remains shared as before; the judge looks into it. If it is suitable to open each in his share without a road, the judge divides without a road, completing benefit and achieving acknowledgment fully. If not, he creates a road between them to achieve completed benefit beyond the road. If they differ on its width, it is made according to the width of the door in length (height) so that each comes out with a wing in his share if it is above the door, not below, because the door of the house is an agreed-upon road, and disputed matters are referred to agreed ones. In this extent is sufficient for entry. And if they stipulate that among them...
Source pages p. 278

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the matn concerning division when one partner has a right of passage (road) or water channel (مسيل) over the share of another. The rule: if the division can be arranged so that the right is redirected away from the other's exclusive share without harming the right-holder, it must be done. If it is impossible to redirect (i.e., the right necessarily crosses the other's share), the division is rescinded (فسخت). The reason: division aims to make each share independent and free from others' rights. If that cannot be achieved, the division fails. This is different from sale, where the buyer's ability to access is not a condition for validity; the buyer takes the property as is, and if access is blocked, the sale remains valid but the buyer may have a claim. The text then discusses cases where the rights are explicitly mentioned in the division: if the partner says 'I give you this with its rights', the right is not necessarily included unless he uses explicit language like 'with its road, water, and channel'. If such explicit language is used, the right is not redirected because it is affirmed. The passage also covers how the road itself is treated in division: it may remain shared if it cannot be given to one partner exclusively. The judge may create a new common road if needed. The width of the road is determined by the door width (as an agreed standard). The last sentence is cut off but seems to discuss a condition about the road among the partners. The authority_weight is from the matn and commentary, reflecting standard Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
مسيل (masīl): A water channel or drain that carries water across property.
طريق (ṭarīq): A road or pathway providing access to property.
فسخ (faskh): Rescission or cancellation of the division contract due to impossibility of achieving its purpose.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The division remains valid, and the partner must tolerate the channel.
B) The division is rescinded (faskh).
C) The partner with the channel loses his right.
D) The judge orders one partner to buy out the other's share.

Key Takeaway
In division of property, any pre-existing right of way or water channel must be redirected; if impossible, the division is rescinded.

Partition of Separate Upper and Lower Floors: Value vs. Area
Intra-Hanafi dispute on valuing separate floors in a partition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on partitioning separate floors and explain why Muhammad's value-based method is the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
When floors differ in value, partition by value ensures equity; area-based division is valid but not relied upon.

Co-ownership of a building with separate floors is common. How should such a property be divided among the owners? The Hanafi school has an internal difference: one view uses market value, another uses physical area. This lesson unpacks the dispute and the relied-upon ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the co-owned property types
The passage mentions three scenarios: a lower floor with an upper floor belonging to someone else, a separate lower floor, and a separate upper floor. Recognise that these are distinct units with potentially different market values.
The units are 'separated' (mujarradan) meaning they are not physically merged but are independent spaces.
2
State the two positions
Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that each unit is valued individually and divided by value (qima). Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the second) hold that division should be by area (dhirāʿ).
Both views are within the Hanafi school; this is an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.
3
Identify the mufta bihi
The commentator explicitly states 'wa `alayhi al-fatwa' — the fatwa is on Muhammad's view. Understand that this is the operative ruling in the school.
Al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah also favours Muhammad's view.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Muhammad's view, each co-owner receives a share equal in value, even if area differs. Under Imam's view, they receive equal area, which may not be equal in value. This practical difference is the key consequence.
The thamarah al-khilaf (fruit of disagreement) determines which ruling a mufti applies in real cases.
5
Evaluate the reasoning (talil)
The text cuts off, but the underlying rationale: area is objective and avoids valuation disputes, but value reflects economic reality. Muhammad's view prioritizes equitable outcome over simplicity.
No explicit response from Muhammad to the opponents is given in this excerpt.

قال رحمه الله : (سفل له على وسفل مجرد وعلو مجرد قوم كل على حدة وقسم بالقيمة) وهذا قول محمد وعليه الفتوى وقال الإمام والثاني : يقسم بالذرع لأن القسمة بالذرع هي

This is the saying of Muhammad and upon it is the fatwa. And Imam (Abu Hanifa) and the second (Abu Yusuf) said: it is divided by area (dhira'), because division by area is...
Source pages p. 279

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the method of partitioning a property that consists of distinct vertical units: a lower floor (sifl) that has an upper floor ('ulu) belonging to someone else, a separate lower floor, and a separate upper floor. The matn from Kanz al-Daqa'iq states that each unit is valued separately, and the partition is carried out based on value (qima), not physical area. The commentator explains that this is the opinion of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, and the fatwa is upon this view. Abu Hanifa (Imam) and Abu Yusuf (al-Thani) hold that the partition should be by area (dhira'), i.e., measuring the square footage of each unit. The text cuts off, but the reasoning likely follows: division by area is simpler and avoids the complexities of valuation. However, Muhammad's view takes into account that different floors have different market values even if equal in area; thus, value-based partition is more equitable. The fatwa is on Muhammad's view, indicating it is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
سفل (sifl): The lower floor or ground floor of a building.
علو (ʿuluww): The upper floor or story of a building.
قيم (qīm): Value; valuation.
ذرع (dhirāʿ): Linear measure (cubit); used here to mean area measured in cubits.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) By auctioning the whole property.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's relied-upon method for partitioning separate floors is by market value, not area, to ensure equity among co-owners.

Dispute on Dividing Upper and Lower Portions of a Property
Intra-Hanafi dispute on division method for mixed-benefit property.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on dividing a property with upper and lower portions and identify which is the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
When dividing property with different benefits, value-based division prevails over area-based division.

When a property includes both a lower part (with extra benefits like a well or stable) and an upper part (only for dwelling), how should partners divide it? The Hanafi school has three answers, each from a founding imam. This lesson unpacks their reasoning and points to the ruling relied upon for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the property type
Recognize that the property consists of a lower part (sufl) with multiple utilities and an upper part (uluww) only for dwelling. This difference in benefits is the key.
Lower part often includes well, stable, cellar; upper part only dwelling.
2
State the three Hanafi positions
List the three views: Imam Abu Hanifa divides by cubit with 1 lower = 2 upper; Imam Abu Yusuf divides by cubit equally (1:1); Imam Muhammad divides by value (qimah).
The text explicitly states each position.
3
Explain each imam's reasoning
Abu Hanifa argues the lower has more benefits so it deserves twice the measure; Abu Yusuf says the essential dwelling benefit is equal; Muhammad argues that because lower and upper are like different types (due to different benefits), equality can only be achieved through value.
Imam Muhammad's reasoning is based on the principle that different types require value adjustment.
4
Identify the mufta bihi position
The text states: 'وهذا قول محمد وعليه الفتوى' – Imam Muhammad's view is the operative ruling for fatwa.
Despite Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf's views being from Zahir al-Riwayah, the fatwa follows Muhammad.
5
Apply to a sample scenario
Practice with numbers: e.g., lower value 200 per sq cubit, upper 100 per sq cubit. Use Muhammad's method to equalize value by adjusting area.
The text gives calculation examples for each imam.

قال رحمه الله : (سفل له علو وسفل مجرد وعلو مجرد قوم كل على حدة وقسم بالقيمة) وهذا قول محمد وعليه الفتوى وقال الإمام والثاني : يقسم بالذرع لأن القسمة بالذرع هي الأصل في المذروع والكلام فيه والعبرة للتسوية في أصل السكنى كما في المرافق. قال في العناية : وصورتها علو مشترك بين رجلين وسفله لآخر وسفل مشترك بينهما وعلو لآخر وبيت كامل مشترك بينهما والكل في دار واحد أو في دارين قيدنا بهذا لئلا يقال قسمة مع السفل قسمة واحدة إذا كانت البيوت متفرقة لا يصح عند الإمام؛ لمحمد أن السفل العلو يصلح منفعة وتفسير لما لا يصلح له العلو كالبئر والاصطبل والسرداب وغيره فصار كالجنسين فلا يمكنه التعديل إلا بالقسمة وكيفية القسمة على قول الإمام ذراع سفل بذراعين من العلو. وقال أبو يوسف : ذراع بذراع قيل أجاب كل منهما على عادة أهل عصره، وقيل هو اختلاف حجة بينهم . قال الإمام : لصاحب السفل منافع كثيرة ولصاحب العلو منفعة واحدة وهي السكني. وأبو يوسف قال : هما سواء في الانتفاع وتفسير المسألة على قول الإمام أن يجعل بمقابلة مائة ذراع من العلو المجرد ثلاثة وثلاثون وثلث ذراع من البيت الكامل فثلاثة وثلاثون وثلث لمن العلو الكامل بمقابلة مثله من العلو المجرد وثلاثة وثلثون وثلث من السفل الكامل في مقابلة ست وستين وثلاثين من العلو المجرد فذلك تمام مائة ويجعل بمقابلة مائة ذراع من السفل المجرد ستة وستين وثلثا ذراع من البيت الكامل لأن علوه مثل نصف سفله فستة وستون وثلثان من سفل الكامل في مقابلة مثله من السفل المجرد وستة وستون وثلثان من العلو الكامل في مقابلة ثلاثة وثلاثين وثلث ذراع من السفل المجرد فذلك تمام مائة . قول الإمام أبي يوسف أن يجعل بمقابلة شيء من السفل المجرد أو من العلو المجرد قدر نصفه من البيت الكامل. ويقابل نصف العلو بنصف السفل لاستواء العلو والسفل عنده ويجعل بمقابلة شيء من السفل المجرد قدره من العلو المجرد. وقال محمد: يقسم على قيمة السفل والعلو، فإن كان قيمتها على السواء يحسب ذراع بذراع وإن كان قسمة أحدهما أعلى من الآخر يحسب الذي قيمته أعلى على النصف ذراع بذراعين من الآخر حتى يستويا في القيمة . وفي الذخيرة فإن قيل : كيف يقسم العلو من السفل قسمة واحدة عند الإمام ومن مذهبه أن البيوت المتفرقة لا تقسم قسمة واحدة إن لم تكن في دار واحدة؟ قلنا : موضوع المسألة أنهما في دار واحدة والبنيان في دار ،واحدة وإنما يقسم عند الإمام رضي الله تعالى عنه وإن كان في دارين بطريق التراضي فلهذا قيد في النهاية بما سبق وعلم من قوله «قوم كل على حدة» أن البناء لا يقسم بالذراع قال : وإن قسما داراً فإنه يقسم العرصة بالذراع ويقسم البناء بالقيمة . ثم هذا على ثلاثة أوجه : فتارة يقسما الأرض نصفين ويشترطا أن من وقع البناء في نصيبه يعطي لصاحبه نصف قيمة البناء وقيمة البناء معلومة أو اقتسموا ذلك وقيمة البناء غير معلومة بأن اقتسموا الأرض ولم يقتسموا البناء، فإن اقتسموا الأرض وشرطا في البناء كما تقدم فيكون بيعاً مشروطاً في القسمة، وهذا البيع من ضرورات القسمة فيكون له حكم القسمة فيجوز وإن لم تعرف قسمة البناء واقتسموا كذلك جاز استحساناً ويفسد قياساً لجهالة
He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: (A lower part that has an upper part, a lower part alone, and an upper part alone: each is valued separately and divided by value.) This is the statement of Muhammad and upon it is the fatwa. Imam Abu Hanifa and the second (Abu Yusuf) said: divide by cubit because division by cubit is the original principle for measured properties, and the consideration is equality in the essence of dwelling, as in facilities. In Al-Inayah: Its form: an upper part shared between two men and a lower part for another, and a lower part shared between them and an upper part for another, and a complete house shared between them, all in one house or two houses; we restrict it with this lest it be said division with the lower part is one division when the houses are separate: it is not valid according to Imam Abu Hanifa. According to Muhammad, the lower and upper are suitable for different benefits and the upper is not suitable for what the lower is suitable for, like a well, stable, cellar, etc., so they become like two different types, and adjustment is not possible except by division. The manner of division according to Imam Abu Hanifa: one cubit of lower equals two cubits of upper. Abu Yusuf said: one cubit equals one cubit. It is said each answered according to the custom of their era, and it is said it is a difference of proof between them. Imam (Abu Hanifa) said: the owner of the lower has many benefits, and the owner of the upper has one benefit which is dwelling. Abu Yusuf said: both are equal in benefit. The explanation of the issue according to Imam Abu Hanifa: in lieu of 100 cubits of pure upper, 33 1/3 cubits of the complete house (are given). So 33 1/3 for the owner of the complete upper in exchange for the like of it from the pure upper, and 33 1/3 from the complete lower in exchange for 66 2/3 from the pure upper; thus completing 100. And in lieu of 100 cubits of pure lower, 66 2/3 cubits of the complete house are given, because its upper is like half of its lower, so 66 2/3 from the complete lower in exchange for the like of it from the pure lower, and 66 2/3 from the complete upper in exchange for 33 1/3 cubits from the pure lower; thus completing 100. The statement of Imam Abu Yusuf: in lieu of something from the pure lower or from the pure upper, half its amount from the complete house. And he compares half of the upper with half of the lower because of equality of upper and lower according to him, and in lieu of something from the pure lower, its equal from the pure upper. Muhammad said: divide based on the value of the lower and upper; if their values are equal, reckon cubit for cubit; if the value of one is higher than the other, reckon the one with higher value at one cubit for two cubits of the other until they become equal in value. In Al-Dhakhira: If it is said: how is upper divided from lower in one division according to Imam Abu Hanifa, while his doctrine is that separate houses are not divided in one division if they are not in one house? We say: the subject of the issue is that both are in one house and the building is in one house; he divides according to Imam Abu Hanifa, may Allah be pleased with him, even if in two houses by way of mutual consent. For this reason it was restricted in Al-Nihayah to what preceded. And it is known from his statement 'value each separately' that the building is not divided by cubit. He said: If they divide a house, they divide the land by cubit and divide the building by value. Then this is in three aspects: sometimes they divide the land into two halves and stipulate that whoever gets the building in his share gives to his partner half the value of the building, and the value of the building is known; or they divide that and the value of the building is unknown, such as they divide the land without dividing the building. If they divide the land and stipulate regarding the building as above, then it is a sale conditioned in the division, and this sale is from the necessities of division, so it has the ruling of division and is permissible. If they do not know the division of the building and divide similarly, it is permissible by istihsan and void by qiyas due to ignorance.
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This passage addresses a key intra-Hanafi dispute: how to divide a property that includes both lower (سفل) and upper (علو) parts with different utilities. The matn states that each component is valued separately and divided by value (قيمة) — this is Imam Muhammad's view, and the fatwa is upon it. Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf disagree: they say division should be by cubit measure (ذرع) because the fundamental principle in measured properties is equality of area. However, they differ on the ratio: Abu Hanifa holds that one cubit of lower equals two cubits of upper, because the lower part has more benefits (well, stable, cellar) while the upper has only dwelling. Abu Yusuf holds they are equal in benefit, so one cubit of lower equals one cubit of upper. Imam Muhammad's view is based on value: if values are equal, divide area equally; if one part is more valuable, adjust area so that the total values are equal. The text then explains the calculation methods for each imam in detail. Finally, it clarifies that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, this division is only valid when the units are in the same building; if separate houses, it requires mutual consent. The passage also discusses the treatment of buildings on land: land is divided by cubit, but buildings are divided by value. If the building's value is unknown, it can be divided with a conditional sale, which is permissible by istihsan due to necessity.

Key Terms
سفل (sufl): The lower part of a building, often including spaces like basements, cellars, and stables.
علو (uluww): The upper part of a building, typically used only for dwelling.
ذرع (dhira): Cubit measure; a unit of length used for measuring area in property division.
قيمة (qimah): Monetary value; used to equalize shares when the components have different utilities.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, how should a property with upper and lower portions be divided?
A) By equal area (cubit for cubit).
B) By value, so that each partner receives equal value.
C) By area but with a 2:1 ratio (lower:upper).
D) By area but with a 1:2 ratio (lower:upper).

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi property division, when components have unequal benefits, division by value (قيمة) is the relied-upon method.

Definition and Proof of Tahayyu' (Allocation of Usufruct)
Defines tahayyu' linguistically and legally with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define tahayyu' linguistically and legally, state its proofs from Quran, Sunnah, Ijma', and reason, and identify its conditions and when it becomes obligatory.

Core Idea
Tahayyu' is a binding exchange of usufruct among co-owners, permissible by Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma'.

This lesson unpacks the concept of tahayyu' – a unique Hanafi mechanism for co-ownership where partners divide the use of property by time or space. The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq provides a comprehensive treatment: definition, proofs, conditions, and when acceptance becomes obligatory. Understanding tahayyu' is crucial for properly managing joint assets in Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Tahayyu' is permissible (ja'iz) by consensus. If one partner requests it and the other does not demand physical division, it becomes wajib for the other to accept.
The ruling changes from ja'iz to wajib when requested.
2
Locate the linguistic definition
The term 'tahayyu'' is derived from 'hay'ah' (form/arrangement), meaning each partner prepares and agrees to a specific mode of sharing.
It is tafa'ul from hay'ah – mutual agreement on an arrangement.
3
Locate the legal definition
Tahayyu' is a mu'awadah (exchange) in meaning, not an iqrar (acknowledgment). It applies only to non-fungible assets (like houses, animals) where the substance remains during use.
It does not apply to fungibles (mithliyyat) like grain – those require physical division.
4
Examine the proofs
Quran: she-camel of Salih (26:155) – alternating days for water. Sunnah: Prophet divided camels among three men at Badr, taking turns. Ijma': ummah agreed on permissibility. Reason: joint physical use is often impossible, so division of usufruct benefits all.
The she-camel verse is the primary Qur'anic evidence.
5
Apply conditions and description
The asset must be beneficial while its substance remains. Tahayyu' can be temporal (time-based) or spatial (place-based). It is obligatory when one partner requests it and the other does not want physical division.
Fungible goods (mithliyyat) are excluded from tahayyu'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
روي قال رحمه الله : (ولو نهاياً في سكنى دار أو دارين أو خدمة عبد أو عبدين أو غلة دار أو دارين (صح) يحتاج إلى تفسيرها لغة وشرعاً وشرطها وصفتها ودليلها وحكمها. أما دليلها فقوله تعالى هذه ناقة لها شرب ولكم شرب يوم معلوم [الشعراء: ١٥٥] ومن السنة فما أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام قسم في غزوة بدر كل بعير بين ثلاثة نفر وكانوا يتناوبون في الركوب. واجتمعت الأمة على جوازها ولأن التهايؤ قسمة المنافع فيصار إليها لتكميل المنفعة لتعذر الاجتماع على عين واحدة فكان التهايؤ هنا جمعاً للمنافع في زمان واحد. وتفسيرها لغة فهي مأخوذة من التهيؤ وهو أن يهيء كل واحد منهما لصاحبه ما شرط له. وفي الشارح: الحالة الظاهرة للتهيؤ للشيء وإبدال الهمزة ألفاً فيها، والتهايؤ من الهيئة وهي تفاعل منها وهو أن يتوافقوا على أمر فيتراضوا به. وحقيقته أن كلاً منهم يرضى بهيئة واحدة ويختارها. وأما تفسيرها شرعاً فهي مبادلة معنى وليست بإقرار من كل وجه لأنها لا تجري في المثليات كالمكيل والموزون، وأما شرطها أن تكون العين يمكن الانتفاع بها مع بقاء عينها. وصفتها أنها واجبة إذا طلبها بعض الشركاء ولم يطلب الشريك الآخر قسمة الأصل، وقد يكون بالزمان. وقد يكون بالمكان
It is narrated: He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And if they enter into a tahayyu' regarding the dwelling in a house or two houses, or the service of a slave or two slaves, or the rent of a house or two houses, it is valid.) It needs explanation: linguistically and legally, its conditions, its description, its proof, and its ruling. As for its proof: Allah's statement 'This she-camel has a drink and you have a drink on a known day' (Surah ash-Shu'ara 26:155). And from the Sunnah: the Prophet (peace be upon him) divided in the battle of Badr each camel among three men, and they used to take turns riding. And the ummah has agreed upon its permissibility. And because tahayyu' is a division of usufruct, it is resorted to for completing the benefit, since it is impossible for all to utilize a single [physical] object simultaneously. Thus tahayyu' here is a collection of benefits in one time. Its linguistic interpretation: it is derived from al-tahayyu', which is that each one prepares for his partner what was stipulated for him. In the commentator: the apparent state of readiness for something, and the replacement of the hamza with an alif, and tahayyu' is from al-hay'ah (form), it is tafa'ul from it, meaning they agree upon a matter and are content with it. Its reality is that each of them is pleased with one specific arrangement and chooses it. As for its legal interpretation: it is a mu'awadah (exchange) in meaning, and not iqrar (acknowledgment) in every respect because it does not apply to fungible things (mithliyyat) like measured and weighed items. As for its condition: that the object can be benefited from while its substance remains. Its description: it is obligatory [to accept] if requested by some partners and the other partner does not request division of the physical asset. It can be temporal (by time) or spatial (by place).
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of the chapter on tahayyu' from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, expanding the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The author states that tahayyu' (the mutual allocation of usufruct among co-owners) requires explanation in terms of its definition, proof, conditions, description, and ruling. The proof for its permissibility is primarily the Quranic verse about the she-camel of Prophet Salih, where the water was shared between his people and the she-camel on alternate days. This is a classic example of temporal allocation of usufruct. The Sunnah evidence is the Prophet's division of camels among three companions in the Battle of Badr, where they rode in turns. There is also consensus (ijma) of the ummah on its permissibility. Rational proof: since joint physical use of a single asset is often impossible, dividing the usufruct (by time or space) allows each co-owner to benefit fully. Linguistically, tahayyu' is derived from 'hay'ah' (form/arrangement), meaning they agree on one mode of sharing. Legally, it is considered an exchange (mubadalah) in meaning, not a pure acknowledgment (iqrar), because it cannot apply to fungible goods (like grains) which are measured or weighed—those must be physically divided. The condition: the asset must be usable while preserving its substance (non-fungible). The description: it is wajib (obligatory) for a partner to accept if requested by another partner who does not want physical division. It can be by time (e.g., one month each) or by place (e.g., each uses a different part of the house).

Key Terms
التهايؤ (al-tahayyu'): A mutual agreement among co-owners to divide the usufruct of a jointly owned property temporally or spatially, without physically dividing the property itself.
قسمة المنافع (qismat al-manāfi'): Division of the benefits or usufruct rather than physical division of the asset.
مبادلة (mubādalah): An exchange; in this context, tahayyu' is considered an exchange of usufruct in meaning, not a mere acknowledgment of shares.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does tahayyu' become wajib?
A) Whenever the asset is jointly owned.
B) When one partner requests it and the other does not request physical division.
C) Only if both partners agree to it voluntarily.
D) When the asset is fungible (mithli).

Key Takeaway
Tahayyu' is a binding, Shariah-sanctioned allocation of usufruct among co-owners, permissible by Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma', and obligatory when one partner requests it and the other does not demand physical division.

Tahayyu': Legal Nature, Intra-Hanafi Dispute, and Specific Rulings
Explains when tahayyu' is iqrar vs mubadala, intra-Hanafi dispute, and liability rules

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi classification of tahayyu' (iqrar vs mubadala), state the intra-Hanafi dispute on forced tahayyu' for slaves, and apply the rulings on death, building, and liability.

Core Idea
Tahayyu' is binding and classified as iqrar for same-type property and mubadala for different types; for slaves, the judge can compel it despite Imam Abu Hanifa's objection.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq delves into the legal nature of tahayyu'—the mutual allocation of usufruct among co-owners. Hanafi scholars debate whether it is a mere affirmation of shares (iqrar) or an exchange (mubadala). They also discuss when a judge can impose tahayyu' against a partner's will, with a notable intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Additionally, practical rulings on death, construction, and liability are provided. Mastering these distinctions is essential for correctly applying partnership law in daily life.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types of tahayyu'
Spatial (place) versus temporal (time). Spatial tahayyu' occurs when each partner uses a separate part of the property; temporal tahayyu' involves taking turns using the whole.
2
Classify the nature based on property type
If the co-owned property is of one type (jins) and the benefit is equal or nearly equal, tahayyu' is iqrar (affirmation). If the property types differ (e.g., house and slaves), it is mubadala (exchange) and requires explicit consent.
The classification determines the rules of riba and the need for consent.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on forced tahayyu' for slaves
The two companions (Sahibayn) allow the judge to compel a partner to accept tahayyu' of two slaves' service, analogizing to physical division. Imam Abu Hanifa requires mutual consent because slaves are not subject to compulsory division. The relied-upon view (asahh) follows the companions.
The key difference is the degree of disparity in service vs. physical value.
4
Understand rulings on death and annulment
Tahayyu' is not invalidated by the death of one or both partners. If one partner later demands physical division (qisma), it takes precedence over tahayyu' because it is 'more comprehensive'.
5
Apply liability rules for use and construction
Placing objects or tying animals in one's allocated space does not create liability for harm to third parties, as it is normal use. But building or digging a well in one's share that encroaches on the partner's share creates liability for that portion.
The distinction is between ordinary use and permanent alteration.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتكلم العلماء فقالوا : إن جرت في الجنس الواحد والمنفعة متساوية أو تفاوتاً تفاوتاً يسيراً فهي إقرار وإن جرت في الجنس المختلف كالدار والعبيد يعتبر مبادلة من كل وجه حتى لا يجوز من غير رضاهم. وفي الكافي : ولا يبطل التهايؤ بموت أحدهما ولا بموتهما ا هـ . ولو طلب أحد الشريكين القسمة والآخر المهايأة يقسم القاضي لأنه أبلغ ولو وقع التهايؤ فيما يحتمل القسمة ثم طلب أحدهما القسمة يقسم ويبطل التهايؤ لأنه أبلغ، في البعض والعارية غير لازمة والمهايأة لازمة؟ فإن قيل جمع المنافع الشائعة في السن في بيت واحد محلل لعدم جواز انتقال العرض من محل إلى محل آخر فكيف يمكن القاضي جمعها؟ فالجواب أن المراد ليس للقاضي أن يجمعها حقيقة حتى يتوجه ما ذكر، بل المراد أن القاضي يعتبرهما جميعاً ضرورة ا والأوجه أنه إقرار من كل وجه في التهايؤ في المكان ولهذا لا يشترط التأقيت وفي المهايأة في الزمان إقرار من كل وجه. ولو أشغل أحدهما نصيبه جاز شرط في المهايأة أو لم يشترط لأنه يجوز المهايأة في الاشتغال حال الانفراد فيجوز تبعاً للمهايأة في السكنى؛ كذا في المحيط . ولو نهاياً في دارين جاز ويجبر الآبي عنها ويعتبر إفرازاً كالأعيان المتفاوتة، فلو وضع أحدهما في داره شيئاً أو ربط فيها دابة فعثر به إنسان ومات لا يضمن، ولو بنى أو حفر فيها بئراً ضمن لأن الأول من مرافق السكني حتى يملكه المستعير فلا يكون متعدياً في نصيب شريكه فلا يضمن وفي البناء والحفر يكون في مقدار نصيب شريكه فيضمن ولا يضمن مقدار نصيبه . ولو تهايآ في دارين على أن يسكن كل واحد منهما داراً أو يؤجرها وإن زادت غلة أحدهما لا يشارك الآخر في الفضل . والفرق أن في الدارين أمكن تصحيح قسمة المنفعة حقيقة، ولو تهايأ في الزمان في الخدمة عبداً جاز لأنها متعينة فيه لتعذر التهايؤ في المكان والبيت الصغير كالعبد. ولو اختلفا في التهايؤ من حيث الزمان والمكان في محل يحتملهما يأمرهم القاضي بالاتفاق، فإن اختاروا من حيث الزمان يقرع في البداية تطييباً لقلوبهما ونفياً للتهمة عن نفسه، ولو تهايآ في عبدين على الخدمة جاز، أما عندهما فظاهر لأن قسمة الرقيق جائزة عندهما فكذا المنفعة. وأما عند الإمام فروي عنه أنها لا تجوز إلا بالتراضي لأن قسمة الرقيق لا يجري فيها الجبر عنده فكذا المهاياة . والأصح أن القاضي يهايؤ بينهما جبراً بطلب أحدهما لأن المنافع من حيث الخدمة قلما تتفاوت بخلاف أعيان الرقيق لأنها تتفاوت تفاوتاً فاحشاً على ما بينا ولو نهاياً على أن نفقة كل عبد على من يخدمه جاز استحساناً لأن العادة جرت بالتسامح فيها بخلاف كسوة المماليك لأنها لا تسامح فيها عادة، وقيد بقوله «خدمة عبد لأنه لا يجوز التهايؤ في غلة عبد واحد؛ كذا في
And the scholars spoke: if it (tahayyu') occurs within one type (jins) and the benefit is equal or only slightly different, it is iqrar (affirmation). If it occurs with different types, like a house and slaves, it is considered a mubadala (exchange) in every respect, so it is not permissible without their consent. In al-Kafi: Tahayyu' is not invalidated by the death of one of them, nor by the death of both. End. And if one of the two partners requests division and the other requests tahayyu', the judge divides (the physical property) because it is more comprehensive. And if tahayyu' occurred in something that is susceptible to division, then one requests division, he divides and the tahayyu' is annulled because division is more comprehensive. But if they make tahayyu' in the dwelling of a single house, such that one lives in one part and the other in another part, or one lives upstairs and the other downstairs, it is permissible, because division in this manner is permissible, and so is tahayyu'. And it is iqrar, not mubadala, because mubadala is not permissible within a single type due to riba. And it was said: it is iqrar in one aspect and 'ariya (loan) in another. And it is not hidden that both of these statements are problematic because each one leaves his right to the benefit in what his partner takes in exchange for the benefit of his share, so how can it be imagined that it is iqrar in its entirety or 'ariya in part? Since 'ariya is not binding, and tahayyu' is binding. If it is said: gathering the common benefits in a single house is problematic because it is not permissible for an 'arad (usufruct) to transfer from one place to another, so how can the judge gather them? The answer: what is intended is not that the judge actually gathers them such that the objection applies, but rather the judge considers them both out of necessity. And the more correct view is that it is iqrar in every respect in tahayyu' regarding place, hence no time limit is required, and in tahayyu' regarding time it is iqrar in every respect. And if one of them puts something in his share, or ties an animal there, and a person stumbles on it and dies, he is not liable. But if he built or dug a well, he is liable, because the first is among the necessaries of dwelling, so he does not become a transgressor regarding his partner's share, so he is not liable. In building and digging, he encroaches on his partner's share, so he is liable for that amount, but not for his own share. And if they make tahayyu' regarding two houses such that each lives in one house or rents it out, even if the rent of one is higher, the other does not share in the excess. The difference is that with two houses, a true division of usufruct is possible. And if they make a temporal tahayyu' regarding the service of a single slave, it is permissible, because it is determined in time, due to the impossibility of spatial tahayyu'. And a small house is like a slave. And if they disagree regarding tahayyu' in terms of time and place in a place that can accommodate both, the judge orders them to agree. If they choose time, he draws lots at the beginning to please their hearts and remove suspicion from himself. And if they make tahayyu' regarding two slaves for service, it is permissible. As for (the two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is apparent, because division of slaves is permissible according to them, and so is the usufruct. As for Imam (Abu Hanifa), it is reported from him that it is not permissible except by mutual consent, because division of slaves is not subject to compulsion according to him, and so is tahayyu'. But the most sound view is that the judge imposes a tahayyu' between them by compulsion upon request of one of them, because benefits in terms of service rarely differ, unlike the physical slaves themselves, which differ greatly as we have explained. And if they make tahayyu' such that the maintenance of each slave is borne by the one who uses him, it is permissible by istihsan because custom tolerates laxity in that, unlike clothing of slaves, concerning which custom does not tolerate laxity. And he qualified by saying 'service of a slave' because tahayyu' is not permissible regarding the rent of a single slave; thus in [al-Muhit].
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on tahayyu', delving into its legal nature (iqrar vs. mubadala) and a range of sub-rulings. The scholars (the author and earlier Hanafi jurists) discuss that if tahayyu' concerns a single type of property (e.g., both shares are of the same quality of house space), and the benefit is equal or only slightly different, it is considered iqrar (affirmation of original shares) and not an exchange. If the property is of different types (e.g., a house vs. slaves), it is a full exchange (mubadala) and requires consent of all parties. The passage then addresses several specific issues: (1) Death does not annul a tahayyu' agreement. (2) If one partner demands physical division (qisma) and the other wants tahayyu', the judge orders division because it is more comprehensive (absolutely terminates co-ownership). (3) Tahayyu' is permissible even for a single house by spatial division (e.g., floors), and in that case it is iqrar, not mubadala, because an exchange within one genus would involve riba. (4) There is a discussion: some said it is part iqrar, part loan, but the author finds this problematic because tahayyu' is binding while a loan is not. The preferred view is that spatial tahayyu' is iqrar; temporal tahayyu' is also iqrar. (5) Liability: placing an object (like tying an animal) that causes harm does not create liability if it is within the normal use of the dwelling, but building a structure or digging a well does create liability for the portion that encroaches on the partner's share. (6) For two houses, each can use or rent his house independently, and no sharing of differential rent. (7) Temporal tahayyu' for service of a single slave is valid; for two slaves, the two companions permit it, but Imam Abu Hanifa requires consent (no compulsion). However, the most sound view (al-asahh) is that the judge can impose compulsion on request because the service benefit is roughly equal. (8) Expenses for maintenance follow the user by custom (istihsan), but clothing is not included because it does not involve tolerance. (9) Clarification: tahayyu' applies only to service of a slave, not to rent of a single slave (which is forbidden because rent requires specific asset delivery).

Key Terms
إقرار (iqrār): In this context, a legal affirmation of the partners' existing shares; the tahayyu' does not create a new exchange but rather acknowledges each partner's right to use a specific portion of the benefit.
مبادلة (mubādalah): An exchange; in tahayyu' of different types, it is considered an exchange of usufruct rights, requiring mutual consent and valid only if free of riba.
جبر (jabr): Compulsion by a judge to enforce tahayyu' or qisma against a reluctant partner, based on necessity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view (asahh) in this passage, can a judge compel a partner to accept tahayyu' for the service of two slaves?
A) No, because slaves cannot be divided physically.
B) No, because Imam Abu Hanifa requires consent.
C) Yes, because the benefit of service is seldom significantly different.
D) Yes, because the judge can always compel tahayyu'.

Key Takeaway
Tahayyu' is a binding allocation of usufruct; its classification as iqrar or mubadala depends on property type and benefit equality, and for slaves, the judge can impose it by compulsion based on the two companions' view.

Tahaayu in Slave Produce: The Rule and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explaining the permissibility and conditions of tahaayu in ghillah, with a focus on the single vs. two slave distinction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tahaayu in the produce of one and two slaves, and explain the disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Tahaayu in variable income is invalid; equality (mu'aadalah) must be possible.

In this lesson, we examine the conditions for valid tahaayu between co-owners, focusing on the critical distinction between service (stable) and produce (fluctuating). The core issue is whether partners can alternate using a slave's income when the income varies month to month. The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement that illustrates the tension between strict analogy (qiyas) and juristic preference (istihsan).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is tahaayu? It is an agreement between co-owners to alternate using a shared usufruct. Here, the usufruct is the produce (ghillah) of a slave. The text first restricts tahaayu to service, not produce.
The matn explicitly mentions 'service of a slave' as permissible; produce is excluded.
2
State the ruling for a single slave
According to the text, tahaayu in the produce of a single slave is impermissible. Why? Because the income from a slave's labor fluctuates greatly (e.g., one month's rent is not equal to the next), making it impossible to ensure equality between the partners' turns.
The example given: a slave hired in the first month cannot be hired in the second month for the same amount.
3
State the ruling for two slaves and the dispute
For two slaves, Imam Abu Hanifa rules that tahaayu in their produce is invalid, while the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) permit it if the produce amounts are equal. The basis: the difference between two slaves' produce is usually minor and can be equalized, unlike a single slave where the fluctuation is large.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Imam vs. Sahibayn.
4
Analyze the proof structure
Imam Abu Hanifa relies on qiyas: just as a single slave's produce fluctuates greatly, so do two slaves' produce, so the same prohibition applies. The Sahibayn rely on istihsan based on custom: since the difference is typically minor, equality can be achieved, making tahaayu permissible for convenience.
The text cites al-Muhit for the single slave rule and al-Sirajiyyah for a similar permissible arrangement in land cultivation.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The mufta bihi (operative position for fatwa) is the Sahibayn's view: tahaayu in the produce of two slaves is permissible if the produce is equal at the time of agreement.
The text does not explicitly choose, but later sources like al-Hidayah adopt the Sahibayn's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقيد بقوله «خدمة عبد لأنه لا يجوز التهايؤ في غلة عبد واحد؛ كذا في المحيط . وقيد بقوله خدمة عبدين لأنهما لو نهاياً في غلتهما لم يجز عند الإمام، وعندهما يجوز إذا استوت الغلتان ولهما أن تفاوت العبدين في الغلة يسير فيجوز عند الاستواء بخلاف العبد الواحد فإنها فاحشة فإن العبد المستأجرة في الشهر الأول لا يستأجر في الشهر الثاني بمثل ما استؤجر في الأول بل بزيادة وفي السراجية : تحل بين شريكين اقتسما على أن يأخذ كل واحد منهما طائفة ويثمرها جاز ا هـ . وفي المنتقى : جاريتان بين رجلين نهاياً على ترضع هذه ابن هذه سنتين وترضع هذه ابن هذه سنتين جاز قالوا ولا يشبه هذا لبن البقر والإبل وعلل فقال : ألبان الإنسان لا قيمة لها ولا تقسم وألبان البهائم تقسم ولها قيمة. وفي الخانية: رجلان تواضعا في بقرة على أن تكون عند كل واحد منهما خمسة عشر يوماً يحلب لبنها كان باطلاً ولا يحل فضل اللبن لأحدهما، وإن جعله صاحبه في حل لأن هذا هبة المشاع فيما يقسم إلا أن يكون صاحب الفضل استهلك الفضل فإذا جعله صاحبه في حل كان الضمان فيجوز، أما حال قيام الفضل يكون هبة أو إبراء عن العين وهو باطل. وفي الكافي : في غنم بين اثنين واتفقا على أن يأخذ كل واحد منهما طائفة يرعاها وينتفع بألبانها لم يجز، والحيلة أن يبيع حصته من الآخر ثم يشتري كلها بعد مضي نوبته أو ينتفع باللبن بالوزن المعلوم ا هـ وفي الكافي : ولو نهاياً في مملوكين استخداماً فمات أحدهما أو أبق انتقضت المهايأة بخلاف ما إذا استخدمه شهراً إلا ثلاثة أيام لو أبق فيه ثلاثة أيام فإنه ينتقض، ولو أبق أحد الخادمين في خدمة من شرط له الخادم أو انهدام الحائط فلا ضمان عليه ولو ولدت منه صارت أم ولد وانقضت المهايأة ؛ كذا في المحيط . ولو كان بينهما عبد وأمة فتهايا فيهما ذلك ؛ كذا صح في الأصل والتهايؤ في الركوب في دابة واحدة لا يجوز عند الإمام، وعندهما يجوز وظاهر عبارة المؤلف أنه يشترط لصحة التهابؤ اتحاد المنفعة، وفي المحيط ما يخالفه قال في المحيط : ولو تهايآ ومملوك على أن يسكن هذا الدار سنة والآخر يخدمه العبد سنة جاز استحسانا ا هـ . قال رحمه الله : ( وفي غلة عبد وعبدين أو بغل وبغلين أو ركوب بغل أو بغلين أو ثمر شجرة أو لبن شاة لا يعني لا يجوز في هذه الأشياء التهايؤ. أما في عبد واحد أو بغل واحد فيجوز فلان النصيبين يتعاقبان في الاستيفاء فالظاهر التغير في الحيوان فتفوت المعادلة بخلاف التهايؤ في استغلال دار واحدة حيث يجوز في ظاهر الرواية، وقد مر بيانه. ولو زادت غلة الدار في نوبة أحدهما يشتركان في الزيادة تحقيقاً للمساواة بخلاف التهايؤ في المنافع فتعتبر المعادلة فيها إلا في الغلة، وبخلاف ما لو نهاياً في الاستغلال في الدارين وفضلت غلة أحدهما حيث لا يشتركان لأن معنى الإقرار راجح في الدارين فلا تعتبر الغلة، وأما لو نهاياً في استغلال عبدين أو بغلين فالمذكور هنا قول الإمام، وعندهما يجوز لإمكان المعادلة فيها .
And it is restricted by his statement 'service of a slave' because tahaayu in the produce (ghillah) of a single slave is not permissible. Thus in al-Muhit. And restricted by his statement 'service of two slaves' because if they make tahaayu in their produce, it is not permissible according to Imam (Abu Hanifa), but according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is permissible if the two produce amounts are equal. And according to them, the difference of the two slaves in produce is minor, so it is permissible when equal, unlike the single slave where the difference is great, for the slave hired in the first month is not hired in the second month for the same amount but for an increase. And in al-Sirajiyyah: A transaction is valid between two partners who divide such that each takes a group and cultivates it. Thus in al-Kafi. And in al-Muntaqa: Two slave girls belonging to two men; they make tahaayu that this one nurses the child of that one for two years, and that one nurses the child of this one for two years. It is permissible. They said this is not like the milk of cows and camels, and he explained: Human milk has no value and is not subject to division, whereas animal milk is subject to division and has value. And in al-Khaniyyah: Two men made an agreement regarding a cow such that it stays with each for fifteen days and he milks it; it is invalid. And the excess milk is not permissible for either of them, even if the owner makes it permissible, because this is a gift of an undivided share in something that can be divided, unless the owner of the excess consumed it; if the owner makes it permissible, then the guarantee is valid. As for the case where the excess remains, it is a gift or release from a specific property, which is invalid. And in al-Kafi: Regarding sheep between two persons who agree that each takes a flock to graze and benefit from its milk – it is not permissible. The legal stratagem (hilah) is that he sells his share to the other, then buys it back after his turn passes, or he benefits from the milk by a known weight. Thus in al-Kafi. And in al-Kafi: If they make tahaayu in two owned persons for service, and one dies or runs away, the tahaayu is abrogated. Unlike if he used him for a month less three days, and if he runs away during those three days, it is abrogated. And if one of the two servants runs away during the service of the person for whom the servant was stipulated, or the wall collapses, there is no liability on him. And if she gives birth from him, she becomes umm walad and the tahaayu is abrogated. Thus in al-Muhit. And if they have a male slave and a female slave, and they make tahaayu in them, the same applies. Thus it is correct in the original. And tahaayu in riding a single mount is not permissible according to Imam (Abu Hanifa), but according to the two it is permissible. And the apparent statement of the author is that for the validity of tahaayu, unity of the benefit is a condition. And in al-Muhit there is something that contradicts it. He said in al-Muhit: If they make tahaayu while having a owned person such that one lives in this house for a year and the other serves the slave for a year, it is permissible by istihsan. Thus in al-Muhit. The author (may Allah have mercy on him) said: (And regarding the produce of a slave and two slaves, or a mule and two mules, or riding a mule or two mules, or the fruit of a tree, or the milk of a sheep – no), meaning tahaayu is not permissible in these things. As for in a single slave or a single mule, it is permissible, because the two shares alternate in utilization, and apparent change occurs in animals, so equality is lost, unlike tahaayu in the utilization of a single house where it is permissible in the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah); its explanation has passed. And if the produce of the house increases during the turn of one of them, they share in the increase to achieve equality, unlike tahaayu in benefits where equality is considered except in produce. And unlike if they make tahaayu in utilization of two houses and the produce of one exceeds, where they do not share because the meaning of acknowledgment is predominant in two houses, so produce is not considered. As for if they make tahaayu in utilization of two slaves or two mules, what is mentioned here is the statement of Imam (Abu Hanifa), and according to the two it is permissible because equality is possible therein.
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This passage completes the discussion on tahaayu, focusing on cases where tahaayu is not permitted due to the fluctuating nature of the usufruct. The author begins by explaining the restriction in the matn regarding 'service of a slave' – tahaayu is not valid in the produce (ghillah) of a single slave because the income from a slave can vary greatly month to month, making it impossible to ensure equality between the partners. However, in two slaves, if their produce is equal, the Sahibayn permit tahaayu, while Imam Abu Hanifa disallows it even then, because the potential for inequality remains. The text then cites several authoritative sources: al-Sirajiyyah permits a similar arrangement for agricultural land; al-Muntaqa permits tahaayu for nursing slave girls' children, differentiating human milk (valueless, not subject to division) from animal milk; al-Khaniyyah rules that tahaayu in milking a cow is invalid because it is a gift of an undivided share; al-Kafi prohibits tahaayu in sheep for milk but provides a legal stratagem (hilah) of selling and repurchasing. The passage also addresses the effect of events like death or absconding: if one slave in a tahaayu arrangement dies or runs away, the tahaayu is abrogated. Similarly, tahaayu in riding a single mount is invalid according to Imam Abu Hanifa but valid according to the Sahibayn. The author's statement that tahaayu requires unity of benefit (ittihad al-manfa'ah) is clarified by a case in al-Muhit where tahaayu combines different benefits (residence and service) and is permitted by istihsan. Finally, the matn itself is glossed: tahaayu is not permitted in the produce of one or two slaves, a mule, riding, fruit, or milk of a sheep, because these benefits are variable. However, in a single slave or mule, it is permitted because the two shares alternate in use and the variability is less pronounced. The distinction with a single house is that house rental income is more stable. In case of excess produce in a house during one partner's turn, they share it to maintain equality, but this does not apply to two houses where each is considered separate acknowledgment.

Key Terms
الغلة (al-ghillah): The produce or income generated from a property, such as rent from a slave's labor or milk from an animal.
المعادلة (al-mu'aadalah): Equality in the benefits exchanged between partners in a tahaayu arrangement, a necessary condition for validity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is tahaayu in the produce of a single slave invalid according to all Hanafi scholars?
A) Because a slave is a human and cannot be traded.
B) Because the income fluctuates greatly, making equality impossible.
C) Because tahaayu requires the slave's consent.
D) Because the slave might run away.

Key Takeaway
Tahaayu in variable usufructs is invalid unless the difference is negligible (as in two slaves), where the Sahibayn permit it using istihsan.

Tahaayu in Animals, Milk, and Riding: Case Studies and Hilah
Explaining the permissibility and conditions of tahaayu in animals, milk, riding, and the use of hilah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rules of tahaayu to cases involving animals, milk, and riding, and construct a permissible hilah for dividing milk benefits.

Core Idea
Tahaayu in fluctuating benefits is invalid, but a legal stratagem (hilah) can achieve the desired outcome lawfully.

We now turn to specific applications of tahaayu: sharing a cow's milk, sheep's wool, or riding a mount. These involve benefits that vary in quantity and value, so tahaayu in its raw form is generally invalid. However, Hanafi fiqh provides legal stratagems (hiyal) that allow partners to achieve their goals while avoiding prohibited transactions. This lesson walks through the rulings and the hilah for milk, as well as the dispute on riding.

Guided Path
1
Identify the cases and their rulings
The text discusses tahaayu in a cow's milk, sheep's milk, and riding a mule. For each, tahaayu is ruled invalid because the benefit is variable and cannot be equalized.
Human milk is treated differently because it has no value and is not subject to division.
2
Understand the hilah for milk
The text provides a hilah (legal stratagem) for sharing milk from sheep or cows: each partner sells his share to the other, then buys it back after his turn, or benefits by a known weight. This transforms the transaction into a valid sale.
The hilah avoids the prohibition of gifting an undivided share.
3
Analyze the riding dispute
Tahaayu in riding a single mount is invalid according to Imam Abu Hanifa, but the Sahibayn permit it. The author's statement suggests unity of benefit is a condition, but al-Muhit contradicts by permitting tahaayu combining different benefits (residence and service).
This is another intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
4
Examine the effect of events
If one of the slaves in a tahaayu dies or absconds, the tahaayu is abrogated. Similarly, if a female slave gives birth, she becomes umm walad and the tahaayu ends.
This is because the subject of tahaayu (the slave) ceases to be shared property.
5
Summarize the matn's final rulings
The matn at the end lists specific items where tahaayu is invalid: produce of one/two slaves, mule, riding, fruit, milk of sheep. The exception is a single slave or mule for service, where tahaayu is valid because the benefit is stable.
The commentary adds that for a single house, tahaayu is valid even in produce because house rent is relatively stable.

Source Text

الغلة يسير فيجوز عند الاستواء بخلاف العبد الواحد فإنها فاحشة فإن العبد المستأجرة في الشهر الأول لا يستأجر في الشهر الثاني بمثل ما استؤجر في الأول بل بزيادة وفي السراجية : تحل بين شريكين اقتسما على أن Commentary

Key Terms
الحيلة (al-hilah): A legally permissible stratagem to achieve a lawful outcome while avoiding a prohibited transaction.
المشاع (al-musha'): An undivided share in jointly owned property.

What is the legal stratagem (hilah) for sharing milk from jointly owned sheep?
A) Each partner takes turns milking the sheep daily.
B) One partner sells his share to the other, then buys it back after his turn.
C) They donate the milk to charity and share the reward.

Key Takeaway
For variable benefits like milk, tahaayu is invalid but a hilah (sale and repurchase) provides a permissible alternative, demonstrating the practical wisdom of Hanafi fiqh.
