The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Taha'yu in Profits
Commentary explaining the ruling and dispute over taha'yu in profits

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on taha'yu in profits and explain the reasoning of Imam Abu Hanifa versus the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Taha'yu is a necessity for indivisible benefits, but for divisible profits it is invalid due to inevitable disparity.

In joint ownership, partners may agree on a temporal division (taha'yu) to alternate the use of an undivided asset. However, when the asset generates profits, the permissibility of such an arrangement hinges on whether equality of benefit (mu'ādalah) can be maintained. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq delves into a key intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that taha'yu in profits of living beings is invalid because their changing nature makes equality impossible, while the Sahibayn permit it if the profits are initially equal. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply Hanafi reasoning to partnership cases.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi positions
Identify the two positions: Imam Abu Hanifa rules taha'yu in the profit of two slaves or two mules as invalid; the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) rule it valid if the two profits are equal.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, so both positions are authoritative within the school.
2
Examine the Sahibayn's proof
The Sahibayn argue that equality (mu'ādalah) is possible because the profits can be made equal, and a slight variation (tafāwut yasīr) is tolerable.
They analogize to inanimate property like houses, where taha'yu in use is allowed.
3
Analyse Imam Abu Hanifa's rebuttal
Imam Abu Hanifa counters that living beings (slaves, mules) inevitably change over time, causing gross disparity (tafāwut fāḥish) in profit from one period to the next. Moreover, profit is divisible tangible wealth, so there is no necessity for taha'yu; the partners can simply divide the profit itself.
The key distinction: necessity (ḍarūrah) justifies taha'yu only when actual division is impossible, as in services.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: according to Imam Abu Hanifa, such taha'yu is completely invalid (bāṭil) and must be avoided; according to the Sahibayn, it is permissible provided equality is maintained. In practice, the muftā bihi (relied-upon) position in later Hanafi works may follow the Sahibayn for certain cases.
The text indicates that the more correct view (al-aṣaḥḥ) for using two slaves is permissibility (see the twelve issues summary).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبغلين أو ركوب بغل أو بغلين أو ثمر شجرة أو لبن شاة لا . أن المحيط . وقيد بقوله خدمة عبدين لأنهما لو نهاياً في غلتهما لم يجز عند الإمام، وعندهما يجوز إذا استوت الغلتان ولهما أن تفاوت العبدين في الغلة يسير فيجوز عند الاستواء بخلاف العبد الواحد فإنها فاحشة فإن العبد المستأجرة في الشهر الأول لا يستأجر في الشهر الثاني بمثل ما استؤجر في الأول بل بزيادة وفي السراجية : تحل بين شريكين اقتسما على أن يأخذ كل واحد منهما طائفة ويثمرها جاز ا هـ. وفي المنتقى : جاريتان بين رجلين نهاياً على ترضع هذه ابن هذه سنتين وترضع هذه ابن هذه سنتين جاز قالوا ولا يشبه هذا لبن البقر والإبل وعلل فقال : ألبان الإنسان لا قيمة لها ولا تقسم وألبان البهائم تقسم ولها قيمة. وفي الخانية: رجلان تواضعا في بقرة على أن تكون عند كل واحد منهما خمسة عشر يوماً يحلب لبنها كان باطلاً ولا يحل فضل اللبن لأحدهما، وإن جعله صاحبه في حل لأن هذا هبة المشاع فيما يقسم إلا أن يكون صاحب الفضل استهلك الفضل فإذا جعله صاحبه في حل كان الضمان فيجوز، أما حال قيام الفضل يكون هبة أو إبراء عن العين وهو باطل. وفي الكافي : في غنم بين اثنين واتفقا على أن يأخذ كل واحد منهما طائفة يرعاها وينتفع بألبانها لم يجز، والحيلة أن يبيع حصته من الآخر ثم يشتري كلها بعد مضي نوبته أو ينتفع باللبن بالوزن المعلوم ا هـ وفي الكافي : ولو نهاياً في مملوكين استخداماً فمات أحدهما أو أبق انتقضت المهايأة بخلاف ما إذا استخدمه شهراً إلا ثلاثة أيام لو أبق فيه ثلاثة أيام فإنه ينتقض، ولو أبق أحد الخادمين في خدمة من شرط له الخادم أو انهدام الحائط فلا ضمان عليه ولو ولدت منه صارت أم ولد وانقضت المهايأة ؛ كذا في المحيط . ولو كان بينهما عبد وأمة فتهايا فيهما ذلك ؛ كذا صح في الأصل والتهايؤ في الركوب في دابة واحدة لا يجوز عند الإمام، وعندهما يجوز وظاهر عبارة المؤلف أنه يشترط لصحة التهايؤ اتحاد المنفعة، وفي المحيط ما يخالفه قال في المحيط : ولو تهايآ ومملوك على أن يسكن هذا الدار سنة والآخر يخدمه العبد سنة جاز استحسانا ا هـ . قال رحمه الله : ( وفي غلة عبد وعبدين أو بغل وبغلين أو ركوب بغل أو بغلين أو ثمر شجرة أو لبن شاة لا يعني لا يجوز في هذه الأشياء التهايؤ. أما في عبد واحد أو بغل واحد فيجوز فلان النصيبين يتعاقبان في الاستيفاء فالظاهر التغير في الحيوان فتفوت المعادلة بخلاف التهايؤ في استغلال دار واحدة حيث يجوز في ظاهر الرواية، وقد مر بيانه. ولو زادت غلة الدار في نوبة أحدهما يشتركان في الزيادة تحقيقاً للمساواة بخلاف التهايؤ في المنافع فتعتبر المعادلة فيها إلا في الغلة، وبخلاف ما لو نهاياً في الاستغلال في الدارين وفضلت غلة أحدهما حيث لا يشتركان لأن معنى الإقرار راجح في الدارين فلا تعتبر الغلة، وأما لو نهاياً في استغلال عبدين أو بغلين فالمذكور هنا قول الإمام، وعندهما يجوز لإمكان المعادلة فيها . وللإمام أن التهايؤ في الخدمة جوز للضرورة لعدم إمكان قسمتها ولا ضرورة في الغلة لأنه يمكن قسمتها لأنه عين مال ولأنه يتغير بالاستغلال بخلاف الدارين لأن الظاهر عدم التغير في العقار. وجملة مسائل التهايؤ اثنى عشر مسألة : في استخدام عبد جائز بالاتفاق، وكذا في استخدام العبدين على الأصح وفي استغلال عبد واحد لا يجوز بالاتفاق، وكذا في غلتها، وكذا في سكنى دارين وفي غلتهما خلاف والأظهر أنه يجوز بالاتفاق، وفي ركوب بغل أو بغلين على الخلاف، ولا يجوز في استغلال عبد واحد بالاتفاق وفي بغلين على الخلاف، أما التهايؤ في ثمر شجرة أو لبن غنم فإنها أعيان باقية ترد عليهما القسمة عند حصولها فلا حاجة إلى التهايؤ لأن التهايؤ في المنافع ضرورة بخلاف لبن بني آدم حيث يجوز التهايؤ فيه كما تقدم، وتقدم بيان الحيلة في ذلك
And two mules, or riding one mule or two mules, or fruit of a tree, or milk of a sheep: no. That is in al-Muhit. And it is restricted to the phrase 'service of two slaves' because if they make temporal division in their profits, it is not permissible according to Imam Abu Hanifa, and according to the two disciples it is permissible if the two profits are equal. And they say that a slight difference in the profit of two slaves is permissible when equal, unlike one slave, for the disparity is gross, because a slave hired in the first month cannot be hired in the second month for the same amount but with an increase. And in al-Sirajiyyah: It is permissible for two partners who divide by taking each a portion and cultivating it. And in al-Muntaqa: Two slave girls belonging to two men: they make temporal division such that this one nurses the son of that one for two years, and that one nurses the son of this one for two years: it is permissible. They said: this is not like the milk of cows and camels. And they reasoned: Human milk has no value and is not divided, whereas animal milk is divided and has value. And in al-Khaniyyah: Two men made an agreement regarding a cow that it would stay with each of them fifteen days, and each would milk it: it is invalid, and the excess milk is not permissible for either of them. If the partner makes it permissible, it is because this is a gift of undivided property that is divisible, unless the one with excess has consumed it; if the partner makes it permissible, then there is liability and it is permissible. As for while the excess exists, it is a gift or release from a specific thing, which is invalid. And in al-Kafi: Two partners in sheep agree that each will take a flock, pasture it, and benefit from its milk: it is not permissible. The trick is that he sells his share to the other, then buys it all after his turn passes, or he benefits from the milk by known weight. And in al-Kafi: If they make temporal division in two slaves for service and one dies or runs away, the division is dissolved; unlike if he used him for a month except three days, and he ran away during those three days, then it is dissolved. And if one of the two servants runs away during the service of the one for whom the servant was stipulated, or the wall collapses, there is no liability. And if she gives birth from him, she becomes umm walad and the division is dissolved. And if they own a male slave and a female slave and make temporal division in them, that is correct according to al-Asl. And temporal division for riding a single animal is not permissible according to Imam Abu Hanifa, but according to the two disciples it is permissible. The apparent wording of the author indicates that for the validity of temporal division, unity of benefit is required. But in al-Muhit there is something contradictory: they said in al-Muhit: If they make temporal division of a slave such that this one lives in this house for a year and the other serves him with the slave for a year, it is permissible istihsanan. The author, may Allah have mercy on him, said: (And regarding the profit of one slave and two slaves, or one mule and two mules, or riding one mule or two mules, or fruit of a tree, or milk of a sheep: 'no' means temporal division is not permissible in these things. As for one slave or one mule, it is permissible, because the two shares alternate in taking, but change is apparent in animals, so equality is lost. Unlike temporal division in the use of a single house, which is permissible in the apparent narration, and its explanation has passed. And if the profit of the house increases during one partner's turn, they share the increase to achieve equality, unlike temporal division in benefits where equality is considered except in profit. And unlike if they make temporal division in the use of two houses and the profit of one exceeds, they do not share, because the meaning of settlement is preponderant regarding two houses, so profit is not considered. As for if they make temporal division in the profit of two slaves or two mules, what is mentioned here is the statement of Imam Abu Hanifa; according to the two disciples it is permissible because equality is possible. And according to Imam Abu Hanifa, temporal division in service is allowed out of necessity because division of service is not possible, but there is no necessity in profit because profit can be divided, being tangible wealth, and it changes by use. Unlike two houses, because there is an apparent absence of change in real estate. And the summary of issues of temporal division is twelve: Using one slave is permissible by consensus; similarly using two slaves according to the more correct view; using the profit of one slave is not permissible by consensus; similarly its profit; and living in two houses and their profits: there is disagreement, and the most apparent is that it is permissible by consensus; riding one mule or two mules: there is disagreement; and it is not permissible in the profit of one slave by consensus, and in two mules there is disagreement. As for temporal division in fruit of a tree or milk of sheep, these are enduring tangibles; division can be applied to them when they appear, so there is no need for temporal division, because temporal division is for benefits out of necessity. Unlike the milk of humans, where temporal division is permissible, as has passed, and the explanation of the trick has passed.
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This passage is an expansion from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explaining the rulings of taha'yu (temporal division) in various types of jointly owned property. The commentary covers the matn statement that taha'yu is not permissible in the profit of slaves, mules, riding a mule, fruit of a tree, or milk of a sheep. The author clarifies that in a single slave or mule it is permissible because the two shares alternate in benefit, but change in living beings causes gross disparity. The commentary details intra-Hanafi disputes: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that taha'yu in the profit of two slaves or two mules is invalid because equality is unattainable, while the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) permit it if the profits are equal. The reasoning revolves around the concept of mu'ādalah (equality) and the nature of the property: services cannot be divided, so taha'yu is a necessity; profits are divisible, so taha'yu is unnecessary. The passage also summarizes twelve issues of taha'yu, listing which are agreed upon and which are disputed, including the distinction between human milk (allowed) and animal milk (not allowed, but a trick is provided).

Key Terms
التهيؤ (al-tahāyu'): Temporal division of the use or benefit of jointly owned property, where each owner takes turns benefiting from the entire property instead of dividing it physically.
المعادلة (al-mu'ādalah): Equality of benefit derived by the partners in a taha'yu arrangement; the condition for validity.
الغلة (al-ghalla): Profit, yield, or income generated from property, such as rent or produce.
الضرورة (al-ḍarūrah): Necessity that justifies taha'yu when actual division of the benefit is impossible (e.g., service of a slave).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does Imam Abu Hanifa consider taha'yu in the profit of two slaves invalid?
A) Because slaves cannot be divided physically.
B) Because the Sahibayn prohibited it.
C) Because taha'yu is only allowed in services, not in profits, and equality is impossible due to changes in living beings.
D) Because the profit cannot be estimated.

Key Takeaway
Taha'yu in divisible profits is invalid per Imam Abu Hanifa but permissible per the Sahibayn if equality is maintained; the key is whether the benefit is indivisible (necessity) or divisible (no need).

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Taha'yu for Wearing Two Garments
Intra-Hanafi dispute on taha'yu for garments

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on taha'yu for wearing two garments and explain the reason for the dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Taha'yu on wearing garments is invalid per Imam because of gross disparity in wearing, but the Sahibayn permit it.

The main text on taha'yu did not cover the case of sharing two garments by time. Some Hanafi scholars ruled that such an arrangement is invalid according to Imam Abu Hanifa, while the two disciples (Sahibayn) allow it. This lesson examines the reasoning behind this intra-Hanafi difference and its practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
The act is taha'yu (temporal division) on wearing two garments. The dispute is whether it is permissible.
2
State the Hanafi position
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, it is not permissible.
3
State the opposing view
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold it is permissible.
4
Analyze the dalil
The Hanafi proof: people differ greatly in wearing, causing gross disparity (tafawut fahish). The Sahibayn likely consider the variation tolerable.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if contracted under Imam's view, the contract is invalid; under Sahibayn, it is valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال : ولم يذكر في الكتاب المهايأة على لبس الثوبين قال بعض مشايخنا : لا يجوز عند الإمام خلافاً لهما لأن الناس يتفاوتون في اللبس تفاوتاً فاحشاً؛ في المحيط . لو كان عبدان بين رجلين غاب أحدهما فجاء أجنبي وقاسم الشريك وأخذا عبداً للغائب فقدم الغائب وأجاز فمات العبد في يد الأجنبي فلا ضمان عليه، وإن مات قبل الإجارة بطلت القسمة وللغائب نصف العبد الباقي، وإن شاء ضمن حصته في الميت لشريكه أو للأجنبي القبض ؛ كذا في الأصل . (فروع) قال في نوادر ابن رستم : إذا كان لأحدهما شجرة أغصانها مطلة على قسمة الآخر فله أن يطالبه بقطع أغصانه؛ رواه عن محمد. وروى ابن سماعة عن محمد ليس له ذلك. وفي الذخيرة وبه يفتي وإذا أراد أحدهما أن يرفع بناءه ويسد الريح والشمس على الآخر قال نصر بن يحيى وأبو القاسم الصفار: لصاحبه أن يمنع ذلك. وقال في الفتاوى : ليس له منعه وعليه الفتوى وإذا أراد أن يجعل داره طاحوناً أو مدقاً للقصارين لم يجز له ولو تنور صغيراً جاز والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم بالصواب.
He said: The book did not mention taha'yu (temporal division) regarding wearing two garments. Some of our scholars said: It is not permissible according to Imam Abu Hanifa, contrary to the two disciples, because people differ greatly in wearing. In al-Muhit: If there are two slaves between two men, one of them is absent, and a stranger comes and divides with the partner, and they take a slave for the absent one, then the absent one returns and ratifies it, and the slave dies in the hand of the stranger, there is no liability. If he dies before ratification, the division is invalidated, and the absent one has half of the remaining slave. If he wishes, he can claim his share in the dead one from his partner or from the stranger who took possession. (Branches) It is narrated in Nawadir Ibn Rustam: If one of them has a tree whose branches overhang the property of the other, he has the right to demand that he cut his branches; narrated from Muhammad. Ibn Sama'ah narrated from Muhammad that he does not have that right. In al-Dhakhirah, and with it fatwa is given. And if one of them wants to raise his building and block wind and sun from the other, Nasr ibn Yahya and Abu al-Qasim al-Saffar said: The other has the right to prevent that. And in al-Fatawa: He does not have the right to prevent it, and upon it is the fatwa. And if he wants to turn his house into a mill or a fuller's pound, it is not permissible for him; and if it is a small oven, it is permissible. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This passage covers additional rulings on taha'yu and several subsidiary issues (furu'). First, it addresses taha'yu on wearing two garments: according to some Hanafi scholars, it is invalid by Imam Abu Hanifa's view because of extreme variation in wearing, but the two disciples allow it. Second, a case of two slaves: if one owner is absent and a stranger divides with the present owner, and the absent owner later ratifies, the liability for the slave's death depends on timing. Third, the furu' section includes disputes about overhanging tree branches: one narration gives the neighbor the right to demand cutting, another denies it; the relied-upon position (in al-Dhakhirah) grants that right. Similarly, disputes about raising a building to block light: the earlier scholars say the neighbor can prevent, but the later fatwa (in al-Fatawa) says he cannot. Finally, turning a house into a noisy business like a mill is not allowed, but a small oven is permissible.

Key Terms
التهايؤ (al-tahāyu'): Temporal division of usufruct between co-owners, e.g., taking turns using a jointly owned item.
تفاوت فاحش (tafāwut fāḥish): Gross disparity or extreme difference in value or benefit, which can invalidate a contract requiring equality.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does Imam Abu Hanifa consider taha'yu on wearing two garments invalid?
A) Because garments are not suitable for time-sharing.
B) Because people differ greatly in wearing, causing gross disparity.
C) Because the Sahibayn disagree.
D) Because the book does not mention it.

Key Takeaway
The validity of taha'yu on wearing garments is disputed within the Hanafi school due to the potential for gross disparity in usage.

Subsidiary Cases and Intra-Hanafi Differences on Co-ownership Rights
Subsidiary furu' rulings on co-ownership and property rights

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings on division of jointly-owned slaves, overhanging branches, blocking light, and turning a house into a noisy business, and identify the relied-upon positions.

Core Idea
In co-ownership disputes, the relied-upon fatwa often favors the neighbor's right to cut branches but not to prevent blocking light from a raised building.

The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents several furu' (subsidiary issues) related to co-ownership and property rights. These include a case of division of slaves with an absent owner, disputes over overhanging tree branches, raising a building to block light, and converting a house into a mill or oven. Each has specific rulings and sometimes differing opinions within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify each furu' case
List the cases: slave division, overhanging branches, raising building to block light, and converting house into mill/oven.
2
Extract the ruling for each case
For slave: liability only after ratification; for branches: right to demand cutting (mufta bihi); for building: no right to prevent (mufta bihi); for mill/oven: mill not allowed, small oven allowed.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi differences
Branches: two narrations from Muhammad; Building: Nasr vs later fatwa.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The text indicates 'and with it fatwa is given' for branches (right to demand cutting) and 'upon it is the fatwa' for building (no right to prevent).
5
Apply the general principle
The rulings are based on preventing harm (darar) and maintaining property rights.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال : ولم يذكر في الكتاب المهايأة على لبس الثوبين قال بعض مشايخنا : لا يجوز عند الإمام خلافاً لهما لأن الناس يتفاوتون في اللبس تفاوتاً فاحشاً؛ في المحيط . لو كان عبدان بين رجلين غاب أحدهما فجاء أجنبي وقاسم الشريك وأخذا عبداً للغائب فقدم الغائب وأجاز فمات العبد في يد الأجنبي فلا ضمان عليه، وإن مات قبل الإجارة بطلت القسمة وللغائب نصف العبد الباقي، وإن شاء ضمن حصته في الميت لشريكه أو للأجنبي القبض ؛ كذا في الأصل . (فروع) قال في نوادر ابن رستم : إذا كان لأحدهما شجرة أغصانها مطلة على قسمة الآخر فله أن يطالبه بقطع أغصانه؛ رواه عن محمد. وروى ابن سماعة عن محمد ليس له ذلك. وفي الذخيرة وبه يفتي وإذا أراد أحدهما أن يرفع بناءه ويسد الريح والشمس على الآخر قال نصر بن يحيى وأبو القاسم الصفار: لصاحبه أن يمنع ذلك. وقال في الفتاوى : ليس له منعه وعليه الفتوى وإذا أراد أن يجعل داره طاحوناً أو مدقاً للقصارين لم يجز له ولو تنور صغيراً جاز والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم بالصواب.
He said: The book did not mention taha'yu (temporal division) regarding wearing two garments. Some of our scholars said: It is not permissible according to Imam Abu Hanifa, contrary to the two disciples, because people differ greatly in wearing. In al-Muhit: If there are two slaves between two men, one of them is absent, and a stranger comes and divides with the partner, and they take a slave for the absent one, then the absent one returns and ratifies it, and the slave dies in the hand of the stranger, there is no liability. If he dies before ratification, the division is invalidated, and the absent one has half of the remaining slave. If he wishes, he can claim his share in the dead one from his partner or from the stranger who took possession. (Branches) It is narrated in Nawadir Ibn Rustam: If one of them has a tree whose branches overhang the property of the other, he has the right to demand that he cut his branches; narrated from Muhammad. Ibn Sama'ah narrated from Muhammad that he does not have that right. In al-Dhakhirah, and with it fatwa is given. And if one of them wants to raise his building and block wind and sun from the other, Nasr ibn Yahya and Abu al-Qasim al-Saffar said: The other has the right to prevent that. And in al-Fatawa: He does not have the right to prevent it, and upon it is the fatwa. And if he wants to turn his house into a mill or a fuller's pound, it is not permissible for him; and if it is a small oven, it is permissible. And Allah knows best.

Commentary
This passage covers additional rulings on taha'yu and several subsidiary issues (furu'). First, it addresses taha'yu on wearing two garments: according to some Hanafi scholars, it is invalid by Imam Abu Hanifa's view because of extreme variation in wearing, but the two disciples allow it. Key Terms
الفروع (al-furū'): Subsidiary issues or branches derived from the main legal principles, often dealing with specific applications.
الفتوى (al-fatwā): The formal legal opinion or ruling that is relied upon for practice; here, the mufta bihi.
الذرائع (al-dharā'i'): Preventive measures; here, the principle of blocking harmful activities (like a mill) is applied.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position regarding overhanging tree branches in the Hanafi school according to this passage?

B) The neighbor has the right to demand cutting.
C) It depends on the type of tree.
D) Only if the branches cause damage.

Key Takeaway
For property disputes, the Hanafi school relies on later fatwa which often favors the active right to prevent encroachment (like cutting branches) but does not allow preventing a neighbor from raising his building unless specific harm is proven.

Temporary Allocation for Services vs. Produce
Introduces tahāyuʾ and lists twelve issues with rulings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on temporary allocation (tahāyuʾ) for services and produce, and explain why the ruling differs based on the possibility of physical division.

Core Idea
Tahāyuʾ is permitted only when division is impossible, such as for services, but not for produce which can be divided.

When co-owners share an asset that cannot be physically divided, Islamic law permits a temporary allocation (tahāyuʾ) of its use out of necessity. However, this permission is limited to benefits and usufructs, not to actual wealth that can be split. This lesson unpacks the foundational distinction between service (khidma) and produce (ghalla) and how it determines the permissibility of tahāyuʾ according to the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Define the principle
Understand that tahāyuʾ is a temporary allocation due to necessity when physical division is impossible.
2
Distinguish service and produce
Identify that service (khidma) cannot be divided, so tahāyuʾ is permitted; produce (ghalla) can be divided, so it is not.
3
Examine the twelve issues
Review the summary rulings for various assets (slaves, houses, mules, fruit, milk) to see how the principle applies.
The twelve issues are listed, but only some are detailed.
4
Note the difference of opinion on garments
Recognize the ikhtilaf between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding temporary allocation for wearing two garments.
Imam does not permit due to variation in wearing; Sahibayn permit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب القسمة
وللإمام أن التهايؤ في الخدمة جوز للضرورة لعدم إمكان قسمتها ولا ضرورة في الغلة لأنه يمكن قسمتها لأنه عين مال ولأنه يتغير بالاستغلال بخلاف الدارين لأن الظاهر عدم التغير في العقار. وجملة مسائل التهايؤ اثنى عشر مسألة : في استخدام عبد جائز بالاتفاق، وكذا في استخدام العبدين على الأصح وفي استغلال عبد واحد لا يجوز بالاتفاق، وكذا في غلتها، وكذا في سكنى دارين وفي غلتهما خلاف والأظهر أنه يجوز بالاتفاق، وفي ركوب بغل أو بغلين على الخلاف، ولا يجوز في استغلال عبد واحد بالاتفاق وفي بغلين على الخلاف، أما التهايؤ في ثمر شجرة أو لبن غنم فإنها أعيان باقية ترد عليهما القسمة عند حصولها فلا حاجة إلى التهايؤ لأن التهايؤ في المنافع ضرورة بخلاف لبن بني آدم حيث يجوز التهايؤ فيه كما تقدم، وتقدم بيان الحيلة في ذلك قال : ولم يذكر في الكتاب المهايأة على لبس الثوبين قال بعض مشايخنا : لا يجوز عند الإمام خلافاً لهما لأن الناس يتفاوتون في اللبس تفاوتاً فاحشاً؛ في المحيط . لو كان عبدان بين رجلين غاب أحدهما فجاء أجنبي وقاسم الشريك وأخذا عبداً للغائب فقدم الغائب وأجاز فمات العبد في يد الأجنبي فلا ضمان عليه، وإن مات قبل الإجارة بطلت القسمة وللغائب نصف العبد الباقي، وإن شاء ضمن حصته في الميت لشريكه أو للأجنبي القبض ؛ كذا في الأصل . (فروع) قال في نوادر ابن رستم : إذا كان لأحدهما شجرة أغصانها مطلة على قسمة الآخر فله أن يطالبه بقطع أغصانه؛ رواه عن محمد. وروى ابن سماعة عن محمد ليس له ذلك. وفي الذخيرة وبه يفتي وإذا أراد أحدهما أن يرفع بناءه ويسد الريح والشمس على الآخر قال نصر بن يحيى وأبو القاسم الصفار: لصاحبه أن يمنع ذلك. وقال في الفتاوى : ليس له منعه وعليه الفتوى وإذا أراد أن يجعل داره طاحوناً أو مدقاً للقصارين لم يجز له ولو تنور صغيراً جاز والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم بالصواب.
Book of Division. The imam has [the rule] that temporary allocation in service is permitted due to necessity because division is not possible, and there is no necessity in produce because it can be divided because it is actually wealth and because it changes through exploitation unlike two houses because the apparent is no change in real estate. The total issues of temporary allocation are twelve issues: in using a slave it is permitted by consensus, likewise in using two slaves according to the most sound opinion, and in exploiting a single slave it is not permitted by consensus, and likewise in its produce, and likewise in residing in two houses and in their produce there is a difference of opinion, and the most apparent is that it is permitted by consensus, and in riding a mule or two mules there is a difference of opinion, and it is not permitted in exploiting a single slave by consensus, and in two mules there is a difference of opinion. As for temporary allocation in the fruit of a tree or milk of sheep, they are remaining physical objects, division reverts to them when they occur, so there is no need for temporary allocation because temporary allocation is in benefits out of necessity, unlike human milk where temporary allocation is permitted as previously mentioned. The explanation of the legal stratagem for that has preceded. He said: The author did not mention in the book temporary allocation regarding wearing two garments. Some of our mashāyikh said: It is not permitted according to Imam [Abu Hanifa] contrary to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] because people differ greatly in wearing. In al-Muhīṭ: If there were two slaves between two men, one of them was absent, then a stranger came and divided with the partner and took a slave of the absent one, then the absent one returned and approved, and the slave died in the hand of the stranger, then there is no liability upon him. If he died before approval, the division becomes void, and the absent one has half of the remaining slave. If he wishes, he may hold his share liable in the dead one against his partner or against the stranger who took it. Similarly in al-Aṣl. Branches: He said in Nawādir Ibn Rustam: If one of them has a tree whose branches overhang into the division of the other, he has the right to demand that he cut his branches; narrated from Muhammad. And Ibn Samāʿah narrated from Muhammad that he does not have that. In al-Dhakhīrah, and with it is issued fatwa. And if one of them wants to raise his building and block the wind and sun from the other, Naṣr ibn Yaḥyā and Abū al-Qāsim al-Ṣaffār said: His partner may prevent that. And it is said in al-Fatāwā: He does not have the right to prevent him, and upon it is the fatwa. And if he wants to make his house a mill or a fuller's press, it is not permissible. And if a small oven, it is permissible. And Allah, the Exalted, knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This passage from the Book of Division explains temporary allocation (tahāyuʾ) in the context of shared property. It begins by stating that temporary allocation in service (khidma) is permitted due to necessity, as service cannot be divided physically. However, produce (ghalla) can be divided because it is tangible wealth, so no necessity exists. Real estate like houses is treated differently because it does not change under use. The author then lists twelve issues of temporary allocation, though only some are detailed. For example, temporary use of a slave for service is unanimously permissible, but use of a slave's produce (i.e., earnings) is not. For two slaves, the ruling varies. For fruit or milk from animals, since these are physical assets that can be divided when obtained, temporary allocation is unnecessary, except for human milk where it is permitted by a legal stratagem. The passage also covers a case where an absent partner's share is taken by a stranger; if the absent partner approves, the division is valid, and if not, it is void. Further branches discuss issues like overhanging tree branches, building height, and converting a house into a mill—rulings are given based on differing opinions, with the preferred fatwa noted.

Key Terms
التهايؤ (al-tahāyuʾ): Temporary allocation of shares among co-owners when actual division is impossible due to the nature of the asset.
الخدمة (al-khidma): Service, as a usufruct from a slave, which cannot be physically divided.
الغلة (al-ghalla): Produce or income from an asset, considered wealth that can be divided.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, why is temporary allocation (tahāyuʾ) permitted for service but not for produce?
A) Service is more valuable than produce.
B) Service cannot be divided physically, while produce can.
C) Produce belongs solely to one partner.
D) The Imam prohibited temporary allocation for produce.

Key Takeaway
Tahāyuʾ is a Hanafi concession for indivisible benefits; it does not extend to divisible physical assets like produce.

6 min
Tahāyuʾ in the Case of an Absent Partner
Describes a scenario of division by a stranger in the absence of a co-owner.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on temporary allocation when a stranger divides property including an absent partner's share, and determine liability for loss.

Core Idea
If a partner approves a division made in his absence, it is valid; if not, the division is void and the absent partner claims from the remaining asset.

What happens when a co-owner is absent and a stranger steps in to divide the shared property? The Hanafi school provides a detailed ruling that balances the absent partner's rights with the actions of the present partner and the stranger. This lesson examines a case from al-Muhīṭ that clarifies liability and the option of the absent partner.

Guided Path
1
Understand the scenario
Two men own two slaves; one partner is absent; a stranger comes and divides with the present partner, taking one slave for the absent partner.
2
Analyze the absent partner's approval
If the absent partner returns and approves the division, the division is valid. If the slave dies in the stranger's hand, no liability.
Approval (ijāza) retroactively validates the division.
3
Consider rejection of division
If the absent partner rejects (or dies before approval), division is void. The absent partner gets half of the remaining slave.
4
Determine liability options
The absent partner may hold the present partner or the stranger liable for his share of the dead slave.
Choice (khiyār) between two parties.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب القسمة

Key Terms
الإجارة (al-ijāra): Here, 'before approval' (قبل الإجارة) refers to the absent partner's ratification, not lease.
الضمان (al-ḍamān): Liability for compensation for loss or damage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case from al-Muhīṭ, if the absent partner approves the division, what happens if the slave dies in the stranger's hand?
A) The stranger must pay compensation to the absent partner.
B) The stranger is not liable.
C) The absent partner can demand a refund from his present partner.
D) The division becomes void.

Key Takeaway
An absent partner's approval retroactively validates an unauthorized division, extinguishing liability for subsequent loss.
